## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the instantaneous rate of change of a chemical species' concentration as a function of current concentration and time. The rate law dA/dt typically depends on powers of concentration A, and explicit time dependence may arise from coupled reactions, external forcing, or effective rate expressions after integrating out other species.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction with equilibrium)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (second-order forward with first-order reverse)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction with conservation constraint)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between first and zero order at high concentration)
- Consecutive reaction effective rate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (sum of exponential terms from coupled linear kinetics)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (first-order with time-varying rate constant)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order pathways)
- Half-integer order: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (radical chain reaction kinetics)
- Inhibited reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Power-law with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (general power-law with constant production/removal term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → standard autonomous rate law dA/dt = f(A), suggesting elementary or composite reaction mechanism
- Negative rate values → net consumption of reactant A, positive values → net production or autocatalysis
- Linear relationship dA/dt vs A → first-order kinetics; slope gives rate constant
- Quadratic relationship dA/dt vs A → second-order kinetics or competing parallel pathways
- Rate approaching constant at high A → saturation kinetics, transition from first-order to zero-order (rational function form)
- Explicit time dependence in rate → coupled multi-species system where other species have been eliminated, or externally driven conditions
- Rate that changes sign at specific A value → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium, root of f(A) gives equilibrium concentration
- Product A*(c-A) structure → conservation law constraint where total concentration is conserved, typical of autocatalytic or bimolecular reactions with stoichiometric coupling
